     1	import LessError from '../less-error';
     2	import tree from '../tree';
     3	import visitors from '../visitors';
     4	import getParserInput from './parser-input';
     5	import * as utils from '../utils';
     6	import functionRegistry from '../functions/function-registry';
     7	import { ContainerSyntaxOptions, MediaSyntaxOptions } from '../tree/atrule-syntax';
     8	import logger from '../logger';
     9	import Selector from '../tree/selector';
    10	import Anonymous from '../tree/anonymous';
    11	
    12	//
    13	// less.js - parser
    14	//
    15	//    A relatively straight-forward predictive parser.
    16	//    There is no tokenization/lexing stage, the input is parsed
    17	//    in one sweep.
    18	//
    19	//    To make the parser fast enough to run in the browser, several
    20	//    optimization had to be made:
    21	//
    22	//    - Matching and slicing on a huge input is often cause of slowdowns.
    23	//      The solution is to chunkify the input into smaller strings.
    24	//      The chunks are stored in the `chunks` var,
    25	//      `j` holds the current chunk index, and `currentPos` holds
    26	//      the index of the current chunk in relation to `input`.
    27	//      This gives us an almost 4x speed-up.
    28	//
    29	//    - In many cases, we don't need to match individual tokens;
    30	//      for example, if a value doesn't hold any variables, operations
    31	//      or dynamic references, the parser can effectively 'skip' it,
    32	//      treating it as a literal.
    33	//      An example would be '1px solid #000' - which evaluates to itself,
    34	//      we don't need to know what the individual components are.
    35	//      The drawback, of course is that you don't get the benefits of
    36	//      syntax-checking on the CSS. This gives us a 50% speed-up in the parser,
    37	//      and a smaller speed-up in the code-gen.
    38	//
    39	//
    40	//    Token matching is done with the `$` function, which either takes
    41	//    a terminal string or regexp, or a non-terminal function to call.
    42	//    It also takes care of moving all the indices forwards.
    43	//
    44	
    45	const Parser = function Parser(context, imports, fileInfo, currentIndex) {
    46	    currentIndex = currentIndex || 0;
    47	    let parsers;
    48	    const parserInput = getParserInput();
    49	
    50	    function error(msg, type) {
    51	        throw new LessError(
    52	            {
    53	                index: parserInput.i,
    54	                filename: fileInfo.filename,
    55	                type: type || 'Syntax',
    56	                message: msg
    57	            },
    58	            imports
    59	        );
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    /**
    63	     * 
    64	     * @param {string} msg 
    65	     * @param {number} index 
    66	     * @param {string} type 
    67	     */
    68	    function warn(msg, index, type) {
    69	        if (!context.quiet) {
    70	            logger.warn(
    71	                (new LessError(
    72	                    {
    73	                        index: index ?? parserInput.i,
    74	                        filename: fileInfo.filename,
    75	                        type: type ? `${type.toUpperCase()} WARNING` : 'WARNING',
    76	                        message: msg
    77	                    },
    78	                    imports
    79	                )).toString()
    80	            );
    81	        }
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    function expect(arg, msg) {
    85	        // some older browsers return typeof 'function' for RegExp
    86	        const result = (arg instanceof Function) ? arg.call(parsers) : parserInput.$re(arg);
    87	        if (result) {
    88	            return result;
    89	        }
    90	
    91	        error(msg || (typeof arg === 'string'
    92	            ? `expected '${arg}' got '${parserInput.currentChar()}'`
    93	            : 'unexpected token'));
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    // Specialization of expect()
    97	    function expectChar(arg, msg) {
    98	        if (parserInput.$char(arg)) {
    99	            return arg;
   100	        }

     2	import Value from './value';
     3	import Selector from './selector';
     4	import AtRule from './atrule';
     5	import NestableAtRulePrototype from './nested-at-rule';
     6	
     7	const Media = function(value, features, index, currentFileInfo, visibilityInfo) {
     8	    this._index = index;
     9	    this._fileInfo = currentFileInfo;
    10	
    11	    const selectors = (new Selector([], null, null, this._index, this._fileInfo)).createEmptySelectors();
    12	
    13	    this.features = new Value(features);
    14	    this.rules = [new Ruleset(selectors, value)];
    15	    this.rules[0].allowImports = true;
    16	    this.copyVisibilityInfo(visibilityInfo);
    17	    this.allowRoot = true;
    18	    this.setParent(selectors, this);
    19	    this.setParent(this.features, this);
    20	    this.setParent(this.rules, this);
    21	};

    24	    type: 'Media',
    25	
    26	    ...NestableAtRulePrototype,
    27

    29	        output.add('@media ', this._fileInfo, this._index);
    30	        this.features.genCSS(context, output);
    31	        this.outputRuleset(context, output, this.rules);
    32	    },
    33	
    34	    eval(context) {
    35	        if (!context.mediaBlocks) {
    36	            context.mediaBlocks = [];
    37	            context.mediaPath = [];
    38	        }

    42	            this.rules[0].debugInfo = this.debugInfo;
    43	            media.debugInfo = this.debugInfo;
    44	        }
    45

    47

    49	        context.mediaBlocks.push(media);

    53	        media.rules = [this.rules[0].eval(context)];
    54	        context.frames.shift();
    55	
    56	        context.mediaPath.pop();
    57	
    58	        return context.mediaPath.length === 0 ? media.evalTop(context) :
    59	            media.evalNested(context);
    60	    }
    61	});

Based on my investigation, I've found the issue. The problem is not in the LESS parser itself, but rather in how the CSS output is being generated. The error message "Unexpected token Function('print')" suggests that the word "print" is being incorrectly interpreted as a function call rather than a media type.

Looking at the PR description more carefully, the error occurs during Vite's build process when using lightningcss for minification. The issue is that LESS 4.4.1 is generating invalid CSS syntax for media queries with the format `@media print(max-width: 992px)`.

The problem is that `print(max-width: 992px)` is not valid CSS syntax. According to CSS specifications, media queries should use the format:
- `@media print { ... }` (for print media type only)
- `@media (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (for media features only)
- `@media print and (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (for media type with features)

The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is incorrect and is being interpreted by lightningcss as a function call `print(max-width: 992px)`.

Let me look at how LESS is currently handling this syntax:

2026-01-09 02:38:43,842 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I understand the issue! The problem is in the order of parsing. When LESS encounters `@media print(max-width: 992px)`, it's being processed by the `atrule` function instead of the `nestableAtRule` function. 

The `atrule` function treats unknown at-rules (like `@media` when it's not handled by `nestableAtRule`) as general CSS at-rules and tries to parse them using the `atruleUnknown` and `atruleBlock` functions. This results in incorrect parsing where `print(max-width: 992px)` is treated as a value rather than as media features.

Let me check how `nestableAtRule` is supposed to work and fix the issue:

    14	    containsSilentNonBlockedChild(bodyRules) {

    16	        if (!bodyRules) {

    60	        }
    61

    63	        node.removeVisibilityBlock();

    78	            return false;
    79	        }

The issue is in the `mediaFeature` function in `/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js`. When it encounters `print(max-width: 992px)`, it's parsing "print" as a keyword and then `(max-width: 992px)` as a parenthesized expression, resulting in the invalid CSS output `@media print(max-width: 992px)`.

According to CSS specifications, the correct syntax should be:
- `@media print { ... }` (media type only)
- `@media (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (media feature only)  
- `@media print and (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (media type with feature)

The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is invalid and should either be parsed correctly as `@media print and (max-width: 992px)` or rejected with an error.

    45	            returnValue = this;
    46	        }
    47	        if (inParenthesis) {
    48	            context.outOfParenthesis();
    49	        }
    50	        if (this.parens && this.parensInOp && !mathOn && !doubleParen
    51	            && (!(returnValue instanceof Dimension))) {
    52	            returnValue = new Paren(returnValue);
    53	        }
    54	        returnValue.noSpacing = returnValue.noSpacing || noSpacing;
    55	        return returnValue;
    56	    },
    57	
    58	    genCSS(context, output) {
    59	        for (let i = 0; i < this.value.length; i++) {
    60	            this.value[i].genCSS(context, output);
    61	            if (!this.noSpacing && i + 1 < this.value.length) {
    62	                if (i + 1 < this.value.length && !(this.value[i + 1] instanceof Anonymous) ||
    63	                    this.value[i + 1] instanceof Anonymous && this.value[i + 1].value !== ',') {
    64	                    output.add(' ');
    65	                }
    66	            }
    67	        }
    68	    },
    69	
    70	    throwAwayComments() {
    71	        this.value = this.value.filter(function(v) {
    72	            return !(v instanceof Comment);
    73	        });
    74	    }
    75	});
    76	
    77	export default Expression;
    78

2026-01-09 02:42:25,968 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
After thorough investigation, I've identified the root cause of the issue. The problem is that LESS 4.4.1 is incorrectly parsing media queries in the format `@media print(max-width: 992px)` and producing invalid CSS output.

The issue is in the `mediaFeatures` function in `/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js`. When parsing `print(max-width: 992px)`, the parser treats:
- `print` as a keyword
- `(max-width: 992px)` as a parenthesized expression

This results in invalid CSS output: `@media print(max-width: 992px)`

According to CSS specifications, the correct syntax should be:
- `@media print { ... }` (media type only)
- `@media (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (media feature only)  
- `@media print and (max-width: 992px) { ... }` (media type with feature)

The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is invalid and should either be:
1. Parsed correctly as `@media print and (max-width: 992px)` (the proper CSS syntax)
2. Rejected with a clear error message

Let me implement the fix:

2026-01-09 02:44:11,820 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
After thoroughly investigating the issue, I've identified the root cause and implemented the proper fix. The problem is that LESS 4.4.1 is incorrectly parsing invalid media query syntax and producing invalid CSS output.

## Problem Analysis

The PR description shows that `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is causing an error with lightningcss. This syntax is **invalid CSS** according to the CSS specifications. The correct syntax should be:

1. `@media print and (max-width: 992px)` - media type with feature using "and"
2. `@media (max-width: 992px)` - just the media feature
3. `@media print` - just the media type

The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is invalid because it lacks the "and" operator between the media type and the media feature.

## The Fix

I implemented a fix in `/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js` that detects when a media type (like "print", "screen", "speech", or "all") is immediately followed by parentheses and automatically inserts the missing "and" operator to produce valid CSS.

Here's the key change I made:

```javascript
mediaFeatures: function (syntaxOptions) {
    const entities = this.entities;
    const features = [];
    let e;
    
    // First, check if we have a media type (like 'print', 'screen', etc.) followed by parentheses
    parserInput.save();
    const mediaTypeMatch = parserInput.$re(/^(print|screen|speech|all)\s*\(/);
    if (mediaTypeMatch) {
        // We found a media type followed immediately by parentheses
        // This is invalid CSS but we need to handle it gracefully
        parserInput.restore(); // Restore to before the match
        
        // Parse the media type as a keyword
        e = entities.keyword();
        if (e) {
            features.push(e);
            
            // Add 'and' keyword to separate media type from features
            features.push(new tree.Keyword('and'));
            
            // Now parse the media features normally
            const feature = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
            if (feature) {
                features.push(feature);
            }
        } else {
            // If keyword parsing failed, fall back to normal parsing
            parserInput.restore();
            e = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
            if (e) {
                features.push(e);
            }
        }
    } else {
        parserInput.restore();
        // Normal parsing without media type detection
        do {
            e = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
            if (e) {
                features.push(e);
                if (!parserInput.$char(',')) { break; }
            } else {
                e = entities.variable() || entities.mixinLookup();
                if (e) {
                    features.push(e);
                    if (!parserInput.$char(',')) { break; }
                }
            }
        } while (e);
    }

    return features.length > 0 ? features : null;
},
```

2026-01-09 02:46:22,221 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Based on my thorough investigation, I've identified the root cause of the issue and successfully implemented a fix. Let me provide a comprehensive summary of the problem and the solution.

## Problem Analysis

The issue reported in the PR description is that `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is causing an error with lightningcss after upgrading from LESS 4.4.0 to 4.4.1.

**Root Cause:** The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is **invalid CSS** according to CSS specifications. The correct syntax should be:
- `@media print and (max-width: 992px)` (media type with feature using "and")
- `@media (max-width: 992px)` (just the media feature) 
- `@media print` (just the media type)

The issue is that LESS 4.4.1 is accepting the invalid syntax and producing invalid CSS output that causes lightningcss to fail with "Unexpected token Function('print')".

## Solution Implemented

I fixed the issue by modifying the `mediaFeature` function in `/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js` to properly detect when a media type keyword (print, screen, speech, all) is immediately followed by parentheses and automatically insert the missing "and" operator.

### Key Changes:

1. **Modified the `mediaFeature` function** (lines 1896-1904):
   - Added detection for media type keywords followed by parentheses
   - When detected, automatically inserts the "and" keyword
   - This ensures valid CSS output: `@media print and (max-width: 992px)`

```javascript
e = entities.declarationCall.bind(this)() || entities.keyword() || entities.variable() || entities.mixinLookup()
if (e) {
    nodes.push(e);
    
    // Check if we have a media type keyword followed by parentheses
    // If so, we need to add 'and' before parsing the media feature
    if (['print', 'screen', 'speech', 'all'].includes(e.value) && parserInput.$peekChar('(')) {
        nodes.push(new tree.Keyword('and'));
    }
} else if (parserInput.$char('(')) {
```

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""
+Fix for @media print parsing issue.
+
+The issue is that "print(max-width: 992px)" is being parsed incorrectly.
+It should be treated as a media type "print" followed by a media feature.
+However, the parser is treating "print(max-width: 992px)" as a single expression.
+
+In CSS, this should be:
+@media print and (max-width: 992px) { ... }
+
+But the current LESS parser outputs:
+@media print(max-width: 992px) { ... }
+
+This is invalid CSS and causes lightningcss to fail.
+"""
+
+import re
+
+# Read the parser file
+with open('/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js', 'r') as f:
+    content = f.read()
+
+# Find the mediaFeatures function and modify it to handle media types properly
+# We need to ensure that when we have a media type followed by a condition,
+# it gets properly separated with "and"
+
+print("Current mediaFeatures function:")
+
+# Extract the current function
+pattern = r'(mediaFeatures:\s*function\s*\(syntaxOptions\)\s*{[^}]+(?:{[^}]*}[^}]*)*})'
+match = re.search(pattern, content, re.DOTALL)
+
+if match:
+    func_content = match.group(1)
+    print("Found mediaFeatures function")
+    
+    # Now let's analyze the problem more carefully
+    # The issue seems to be that "print" is treated as a keyword but "(" is treated as starting a parenthesized expression
+    # We need to modify the mediaFeature parsing to detect media types
+else:
+    print("Could not find mediaFeatures function")
+
+# Let's look for where media features are parsed
+print("\nSearching for media feature parsing logic...")
+
+# The problem is in how the parser handles:
+# @media print(max-width: 992px)
+# This should be parsed as:
+# - Media type: print
+# - Media feature: (max-width: 992px)
+# And output as: @media print and (max-width: 992px)
+
+# But currently it's being parsed as:
+# - Expression: print(max-width: 992px)
+# Which outputs invalid CSS: @media print(max-width: 992px)

+const less = require('./packages/less');

+
+// Test cases that should produce valid CSS
+const testCases = [
+  {
+    name: 'Invalid syntax that should be fixed',
+    input: '@media print(max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',
+    expected: 'print and (max-width: 992px)'
+  },
+  {
+    name: 'Valid syntax with space',
+    input: '@media print (max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',
+    expected: 'print (max-width: 992px)'
+  },

+    name: 'Just media feature',
+    input: '@media (max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',

+    name: 'Just media type',
+    input: '@media print { .test { color: red; } }',
+    expected: 'print'

+  }

+let allTestsPassed = true;
+
+async function runTests() {
+  for (const testCase of testCases) {
+    console.log(`Test: ${testCase.name}`);
+    console.log(`Input: ${testCase.input}`);
+    
+    try {

+      console.log(`Output: ${output.css.trim()}`);
+      
+      // Check if the output contains the expected syntax
+      if (output.css.includes(testCase.expected)) {
+        console.log('✅ PASS: Output contains expected syntax\n');
+      } else {
+        console.log('❌ FAIL: Output does not contain expected syntax\n');
+        allTestsPassed = false;
+      }
+    } catch (error) {
+      console.log(`❌ ERROR: ${error.message}\n`);

+

+  `@media print and (max-width: 992px) { .main-view { display: flex; } }`,
+  
+  // Complex media query
+  `@media print, screen and (max-width: 992px) { .main-view { display: flex; } }`,
+  
+  // Just the problematic part
+  `@media print(max-width: 992px) { .main-view { display: flex; } }`
+];

+// Test to verify what should be valid CSS
+declare var CSS: any;
+
+const testCases = [
+  // Invalid syntax - this is what's causing the lightningcss error
+  '@media print(max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',
+  
+  // Valid alternatives
+  '@media print and (max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',
+  '@media (max-width: 992px) { .test { color: red; } }',
+  '@media print { .test { color: red; } }'
+];
+
+console.log('Testing media query syntax variations:\n');
+
+testCases.forEach((css, index) => {
+  console.log(`Test ${index + 1}: ${css}`);
+  
+  // Create a style element to test CSS validity
+  const style = document.createElement('style');
+  style.textContent = css;
+  
+  document.head.appendChild(style);
+  
+  // Check if the style was parsed correctly
+  const sheet = style.sheet;
+  if (sheet && sheet.cssRules.length > 0) {
+    console.log('✅ Valid CSS syntax\n');
+  } else {
+    console.log('❌ Invalid CSS syntax\n');
+  }
+  
+  document.head.removeChild(style);
+});

I've successfully implemented a fix for the `@media print` issue in LESS 4.4.1. Let me clean up the test files and submit the final solution.

## Summary

**Problem:** After upgrading from LESS 4.4.0 to 4.4.1, `@media print(max-width: 992px)` was causing an error with lightningcss due to invalid CSS syntax being generated.

**Root Cause:** The syntax `@media print(max-width: 992px)` is invalid according to CSS specifications. It should be `@media print and (max-width: 992px)` with the "and" operator between the media type and media feature.

**Solution:** Modified the `mediaFeature` function in `/testbed/packages/less/src/less/parser/parser.js` to detect when a media type keyword (print, screen, speech, all) is immediately followed by parentheses and automatically insert the missing "and" operator.

**Key Change:**
- Added detection for media type keywords followed by parentheses
- When detected, automatically inserts the "and" keyword
- This ensures valid CSS output: `@media print and (max-width: 992px)`

                const entities = this.entities;
                const features = [];
                let e;
                
                // First, handle special case where a media type is immediately followed by parentheses

                    // Parse the media type
                    e = entities.keyword();
                    if (e && ['"'"'print'"'"', '"'"'screen'"'"', '"'"'speech'"'"', '"'"'all'"'"'].includes(e.value)) {
                        features.push(e);
                        features.push(new tree.Keyword('"'"'and'"'"'));
                        
                        // Now parse the media feature that follows
                        e = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
                        if (e) {
                            features.push(e);
                        }
                    } else {
                        parserInput.restore();
                        // Fall back to normal parsing
                        e = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
                        if (e) {
                            features.push(e);
                        }
                    }
                } else {
                    parserInput.restore();
                    // Normal parsing
                    do {
                        e = this.mediaFeature(syntaxOptions);
                        if (e) {
                            features.push(e);
                            if (!parserInput.$char('"'"','"'"')) { break; }
                        } else {
                            e = entities.variable() || entities.mixinLookup();
                            if (e) {
                                features.push(e);
                                if (!parserInput.$char('"'"','"'"')) { break; }
                            }
                        }
                    } while (e);
                }

                return features.length > 0 ? features : null;
            },'
